Khiyar al-Bulugh: The Option of Puberty in Hanafi Law
Explaining khiyar al-bulugh, its conditions, and when it lapses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for khiyar al-bulugh and identify when it lapses according to Hanafi law.

Core Idea
A virgin must exercise khiyar al-bulugh immediately upon puberty; any delay or consent makes the marriage binding.

In Hanafi family law, a minor married by a guardian other than the father or grandfather has the right to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty. This right, called khiyar al-bulugh, must be exercised immediately for a virgin girl. This lesson explains the precise conditions, the role of the qadi, and what actions forfeit the option.

Guided Path
1
Identify the marriage scenario
The marriage is contracted by a guardian other than the father/grandfather (e.g., brother) with a compatible match (kafaa). Such a marriage is valid but not binding; the minor has the option upon puberty.
This option does not arise if the father or grandfather contracted the marriage.
2
Determine the puberty trigger
Puberty is determined either by physical signs (e.g., menstruation) or upon completing 15 lunar years if no signs appear. Age is always calculated by the lunar calendar, not solar.
The passage gives an example: if born at sunrise on Ramadan 1, she becomes adult at sunrise on Ramadan 6 of her 15th year.
3
Apply the immediate exercise condition for a virgin
A virgin girl must immediately (without any delay) verbally reject the marriage upon becoming aware of puberty. Any delay voids the option.
The text uses the phrase 'fauran' (immediately) and 'baghair kisi takheer ke' (without any delay).
4
Recognize acts that make the marriage binding
Explicit consent (word or deed) after puberty, consummation, or any delay in rejecting the marriage makes it binding and extinguishes the option.
Silence alone is not sufficient for khiyar; but for a virgin, silence after puberty without rejection is considered a loss of option due to delay.
5
Note the requirement of qadi or substitute
For annulment to take effect, a qadi's decision is necessary. If no qadi exists, a shari'ah committee (panchayat) fulfilling specific conditions can act.
The passage references 'Hila Najizah' for the conditions of the committee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر کفو کے ساتھ ہر شکل پر کیا ہو تو اس وقت نکاح صحیح تو ہو جاتا ہے ولیکن لازم نہیں ہوتا، یعنی لڑکے لڑکی کو بالغ ہونے پر اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ اس نکاح کو باقی رکھیں یا فسخ کرا لیں، جس کی شرط بھی آتی ہے، اور اختیار کو خیار بلوغ کہا جاتا ہے۔ اور خیار بلوغ میں نکاح فسخ ہونے کے لیے ہر ایک حالت میں قاضی کا فیصلہ شرط ہے، قاضی کے فیصلہ کے بغیر کسی حالت میں نکاح فسخ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اور جہاں قاضی نہ ہو وہاں پر سلطان حاکم یا پنجائیت یعنی شرعی کمیٹی جس کی شرائط حیلہ ناجزہ جز دوم کے مقدمہ میں مذکور ہیں علی الترتیب فسخ کر سکتی ہے۔ بالغ ہونے پر فسخ نکاح کا جو بعد بلوغ، فسخ کا کب تک اختیار رہتا ہے اختیار حاصل ہوتا ہے اس میں اس بات کا خیال رکھنا بھی نہایت ضروری ہے کہ وہ کب تک باقی رہتا ہے اور کس کس وجہ سے نکاح لازم ہو کر فسخ کا اختیار باطل ہو جاتا ہے، لہذا اس کی تفصیل بیان کی جاتی ہے تاکہ عمل کے وقت اس کا خاص طور پر خیال رکھا جائے۔ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جو لڑکی بالغ ہونے پر بالغہ ہوتے ہی خیار فسخ استعمال کرنا، نکاح فسخ کرانا چاہتی ہے، اگر وہ بکرہ (کنواری) ہو تو اس کو اختیار فسخ حاصل ہونے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ جس وقت اس پر بالغ ہونے کی علامتیں ظاہر ہوں اسی وقت فوراً کسی تاخیر کے بغیر، زبان سے یہ کہہ دے کہ میں اس نکاح پر راضی نہیں۔ چاہیے اس وقت اس کے پاس کوئی موجود [؟] بکرہ ہونے کا یہ مطلب ہے کہ نہ تو اس شوہر سے ہمبستری کی نوبت آئی اور نہ کسی سے پہلے کسی دوسرے شوہر سے۔ یہ حکم اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ پندرہ سال سے بالغ ہونے کی علامات ظاہر ہو جائیں۔ ورنہ جس وقت پورے پندرہ سال کی عمر ہو جائے تو اس وقت کا اعتبار ہو گا۔ مثلاً کوئی لڑکی رمضان سے ہے کی ہے تاریخ کو مین آفتاب نکلنے کے وقت پیدا ہوئی اور اس [؟] رمضان شہر ایک کوئی بالغ ہونے کی علامت نہ پائی گئی ہو تو سر رمضان شش کو، ٹھیک طلوع آفتاب کے وقت اس کو شرعاً بالغ سمجھا جائے گا۔ پس اگر اس بکرہ نے اُسی وقت فوراً زبان سے نکاح فسخ کر دیا جب تو اس کا اعتبار ہو گا، ورنہ اگر کچھ بھی دیر کی تاخیر کی تو خیار بلوغ باطل ہو گیا۔ اور اسی طرح شبہ [؟] یا لڑکے نے وقت ذکور [؟] بعد قول یا فعلا رضامندی ظاہر کر دی تو نکاح لازم ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ بھی یاد رکھیں کہ عمر کا حساب چاند کے سال سے کیا جائے، انگریزی وغیرہ کا اعتبار نہیں۔
And if it is done in every form with compatibility, then at that time the marriage does become valid but is not binding, meaning the boy and girl upon attaining puberty have the option to keep this marriage or have it annulled, for which a condition also comes, and the option is called khiyar al-bulugh. And in khiyar al-bulugh, for the dissolution of marriage, in every condition the decision of a qadi is a condition; without the qadi's decision, the marriage cannot be dissolved in any situation. And where there is no qadi, the sultan (ruler) or a council (panchayat) i.e., a shari'ah committee, whose conditions are mentioned in the introduction of the second part of Hila Najizah, can dissolve it in order. After reaching puberty, the option to dissolve the marriage—how long does the option remain? It is extremely important to consider how long it lasts and due to which causes the marriage becomes binding and the option to dissolve becomes invalid; hence its detail is explained so that it can be especially kept in mind at the time of action. The detail is that a girl who, upon becoming an adult, wants to use the option of dissolution immediately, if she is a virgin, then for her to have the option of dissolution, the condition is that at the moment signs of puberty appear on her, she must immediately, without any delay, say with her tongue, 'I am not pleased with this marriage.' It is required that at that time she is present [؟]. Being a virgin means that neither has intercourse occurred with this husband nor previously with any other husband. This ruling applies when signs of puberty appear at fifteen years of age. Otherwise, when she completes fifteen years of age, then that time will be considered. For example, a girl was born in Ramadan on such and such date at sunrise, and if in that [؟] Ramadan month no sign of puberty is found, then on the sixth of Ramadan, exactly at sunrise, she will be considered legally adult. So if that virgin immediately dissolved the marriage verbally at that same time, then it will be considered; otherwise, if there was any delay at all, the option of puberty becomes void. Similarly, if [؟] or the boy after [؟] time expressed consent by word or deed, then the marriage becomes binding. Also remember that age is calculated by the lunar year; English etc. reckoning is not considered.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage explains the khiyar al-bulugh (option of puberty) in detail. When a marriage is contracted by a guardian other than the father or grandfather (such as a brother), and it is with a compatible person, the marriage is valid but not immediately binding. Upon reaching puberty, the minor may choose to affirm or annul the marriage. Annulment requires a qadi's decision; if no qadi exists, a shari'ah committee can act. For a virgin girl, the option must be exercised immediately upon the onset of puberty (by signs or upon completing 15 lunar years) without delay; any delay forfeits the option. If she consents explicitly or implicitly after puberty, the marriage becomes binding. The calculation of age is by lunar calendar, not solar. This ruling is crucial in legal stratagems (hilal) where the option is used to escape an unwanted marriage.

Key Terms
بکرہ (bikr): A virgin girl who has never been married nor had sexual intercourse
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of puberty: the right of a minor married by a guardian other than father/grandfather to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a virgin girl, upon reaching puberty, delays even a moment before expressing rejection of a marriage contracted by her brother?
A) She can still annul the marriage within three days
B) The marriage becomes binding and her option is lost
C) She must go to court immediately
D) She can annul by remaining silent

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a virgin must exercise khiyar al-bulugh immediately upon reaching puberty; any delay or consent makes the marriage binding.

Khiyar al-Bulugh: Conditions for Virgin and Non-Virgin
Explaining the rules for khiyar al-bulugh for virgin and non-virgin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules of khiyar al-bulugh to determine the validity of the option for a virgin, non-virgin, or boy.

Core Idea
For a virgin, the option vanishes with delay; for a non-virgin or boy, it lasts until explicit consent.

The option of annulment upon puberty (khiyar al-bulugh) is a special right granted to minors who were married before puberty. This lesson focuses on the critical distinction between a virgin and a non-virgin (or a boy) regarding the duration of this option. The rulings are precise and depend on immediate action or express consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the party and status
Determine whether the person is a virgin girl (bakira), a non-virgin girl (thayyiba), or a boy. This classification determines the rule.
A virgin has never had intercourse; a non-virgin has.
2
Apply the rule for a virgin
If the person is a virgin, she must immediately reject the marriage verbally upon reaching puberty (by signs or age 15 lunar). Any delay, even a moment, voids the option.
She should state clearly: 'I am not pleased with this marriage.'
3
Apply the rule for a non-virgin or boy
If the person is a non-virgin or a boy, the option continues until they explicitly consent (verbally or by action). Silence or delay does not invalidate the option.
Explicit consent after puberty makes the marriage binding.
4
Note the age calculation
Puberty is determined by signs or, if none, by completing 15 lunar years. Use lunar calendar (not Gregorian).
For a girl born on Ramadan 1 at sunrise, she becomes adult at exactly 15 Ramadan later at sunrise.
5
Consider the presence of witnesses
For a virgin's immediate rejection, it is necessary that someone be present at the time of statement to serve as witness.
This is for proof, not validity per se, but it is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالغ ہونے پر فسخ نکاح کا جو بعد بلوغ، فسخ کا کب تک اختیار رہتا ہے اختیار حاصل ہوتا ہے اس میں اس بات کا خیال رکھنا بھی نہایت ضروری ہے کہ وہ کب تک باقی رہتا ہے اور کس کس وجہ سے نکاح لازم ہوکر فسخ کا اختیار باطل ہو جاتا ہے لہذا اس کی تفصیل بیان کی جاتی ہے تاکہ عمل کے وقت اس کا خاص طور پر خیال رکھا جائے۔ تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جو لڑکی بالغ ہونے پر نکاح فسخ کرانا چاہتی ہے اگر وہ باکرہ ہو تو اس کو اختیار فسخ حاصل ہونے کے لیے یہ شرط ہے کہ جس وقت اس پر بالغ ہونے کی علامتیں ظاہر ہوں اسی وقت فوراً کسی تاخیر کے بغیر، زبان سے یہ کہہ دے کہ میں اس نکاح پر راضی نہیں ۔ چاہیے اس وقت اس کے پاس کوئی موجود ہو۔ باکرہ ہونے کا یہ مطلب ہے کہ نہ تو اس شوہر سے ہمبستری کی نوبت آئی اور نہ پہلے کسی دوسرے شوہر سے۔ یہ حکم اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ پندرہ سال سے پہلے بالغ ہونے کی علامات ظاہر ہو جائیں۔ ورنہ جس وقت پورے پندرہ سال کی عمر ہو جائے تو اس وقت کا اعتبار ہو گا۔ مثلاً کوئی لڑکی رمضان کی پہلی تاریخ کو طلوع آفتاب کے وقت پیدا ہوئی اور پندرہ سال تک بالغ ہونے کی علامت نہ پائی گئی ہو تو پندرہ رمضان کی پہلی تاریخ کو ٹھیک طلوع آفتاب کے وقت اس کو شرعاً بالغ سمجھا جائے گا۔ پس اگر اس باکرہ نے اسی وقت فوراً زبان سے نکاح فسخ کر دیا تو اس کا اعتبار ہو گا ورنہ اگر کچھ بھی دیر کی تاخیر کی تو خیار بلوغ باطل ہوگیا۔ اور اسی طرح ثیبہ نے یا لڑکے نے وقت بلوغ کے بعد قولاً یا فعلاً رضامندی ظاہر کردی تو نکاح لازم ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ بھی یاد رکھیں کہ عمر کا حساب چاند کے سال سے کیا جائے، انگریزی وغیرہ کا اعتبار نہیں۔
Regarding the annulment of marriage upon reaching puberty: after puberty, how long does the option of annulment remain? It is essential to know how long it lasts and due to what reasons the marriage becomes binding and the option expires. Therefore, its detail is given so that it may be specially observed at the time of action. The detail is: A girl who wishes to annul the marriage upon reaching puberty, if she is a virgin, then for her to have the option of annulment, the condition is that at the moment signs of puberty appear on her, immediately without any delay, she should say with her tongue, 'I am not pleased with this marriage.' It is necessary that at that time someone be present with her. The meaning of 'virgin' is that neither has intercourse occurred with this husband nor with any previous husband. This ruling applies when signs of puberty appear before the age of fifteen. Otherwise, when she completes the full age of fifteen, that time will be considered. For example, if a girl was born on the first of Ramadan at sunrise and no sign of puberty appeared until fifteen years, then on the first of the fifteenth Ramadan exactly at sunrise, she will be considered legally adult. So if this virgin immediately at that time verbally annuls the marriage, it will be valid; otherwise, if there is any delay, the option of puberty becomes void. Similarly, if a non-virgin or a boy after puberty expresses consent verbally or by action, the marriage becomes binding. And also remember that age is calculated by lunar years; English etc. are not considered.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage is a ruling (rasm) concerning khiyar al-bulugh, the option of annulment upon reaching puberty. It clarifies the duration of the option and the conditions for its exercise. The author distinguishes between a virgin (bakira) and a non-virgin (thayyiba) or a boy. For a virgin, the option must be exercised immediately upon attaining puberty, whether by physical signs or by reaching the age of fifteen lunar years. Verbal rejection is required, and it must be done without delay. Any delay, even a moment, voids the option. Witnesses are also mentioned as necessary for proof. For a non-virgin (a girl who has previously had intercourse) and for a boy, the option remains until they explicitly express consent, either verbally or through action. Mere silence or delay does not invalidate the option. This is a well-established Hanafi rule from Zahir al-Riwayah. The passage also notes the use of lunar years for calculating age, a point often overlooked.

Key Terms
خیار بلوغ (khiyar al-bulugh): The option of annulment granted to a minor upon reaching puberty regarding a marriage contracted during minority.
باکرہ (bakira): A virgin girl who has never had intercourse, whether with the current husband or a previous one.
ثیبہ (thayyiba): A non-virgin girl who has had intercourse, either with the current husband or a previous one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A girl reaches puberty at age 12. She is a virgin. She remains silent for one hour and then says she does not consent. According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling?
A) Her option is still valid because she expressed dissent within the same day.
B) Her option is void because she delayed, and immediate rejection was required.
C) Her option is void only if she had sexual experience.
D) Her option remains valid until she explicitly consents.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the exercise of khiyar al-bulugh hinges on the status of the person: a virgin must act immediately, while a non-virgin or boy has a continuing option until explicit consent.

Scenarios of Marriage to a Non-Compatible Spouse
Classifying rulings on marriages with non-compatible spouses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the four scenarios of marriage to a non-compatible spouse (ghayr kuf) and state whether each is void or valid and binding, and identify the conditions for the option of rescission (khiyar fasakh).

Core Idea
A marriage to a non-compatible spouse without guardian permission is void; only marriage by a sound father or grandfather can be binding despite non-compatibility.

In Hanafi family law, the concept of kafa'ah (compatibility) is crucial for the validity of marriage when guardian permission is lacking. This passage from Al-Hilat al-Najijah systematically classifies four scenarios involving ghayr kuf marriages, distinguishing between void, valid-but-not-binding, and valid-and-binding unions. Understanding these categories is essential for a mufti when determining the need for judicial annulment or the validity of an existing marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
Read the text and list the four distinct forms of marriage to a non-compatible spouse described by the author.
Focus on the parties involved (woman, guardian, minor) and their conditions (maturity, knowledge, probity).
2
Classify each ruling
For each scenario, determine whether the marriage is batil (void), sahih lazim (valid and binding), or sahih ghayr lazim (valid but rescindable).
The text explicitly states the ruling for each scenario.
3
Extract the key conditions
Note the conditions that affect the ruling: guardian type (father/grandfather vs. others), woman's maturity, knowledge of non-compatibility, and father's probity (being fasiq mutahattik).
These conditions determine the classification.
4
Apply the khiyar fasakh principle
Identify which scenarios allow the option of rescission (khiyar fasakh) and which do not. The text notes that the purpose is to highlight where judicial annulment (qada) is needed.
Only scenarios where the marriage is valid but non-binding give the right of rescission.
5
Relate to mufti's practice
Consider how a mufti would apply these classifications in real fatwa situations, especially regarding the need for annulment or confirmation of validity.
The mufti must ascertain the exact circumstances (guardian type, knowledge, probity) before issuing a ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غیر کفو میں نکاح ہونے کی کئی صورتیں ہیں بعض میں نکاح باطل ہے اور بعض میں صحیح اور لازم ہو جاتا ہے یعنی فسخ کا اختیار بھی نہیں رہتا اور بعض میں تو ہو جاتا ہے مگر لازم نہیں ہوتا بلکہ فسخ کا اختیار رہتا ہے۔ یہاں اصل مقصود تو انہی صورتوں کا بیان کرنا ہے جن میں خیار فسخ ہو کیوں کہ قضائے قاضی کی ضرورت صرف انہی میں پڑتی ہے مگر ہم تمام فائدہ کے لیے سب صورتیں درج کرتے ہیں اور ہر ایک کو جداگانہ کم لکھتے ہیں جن کی تفصیل یہ ہے۔ پہلی صورت یہ کہ بالغ عورت بغیر اذن ولی کے غیر کفو میں نکاح کرلے اس صورت میں حکم یہ ہے کہ نکاح صحیح نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بالکل باطل ہے حتی کہ اگر نکاح کے بعد ولی اجازت دے دے تب بھی صحیح نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ نکاح سے قبل اجازت کا ہونا شرط ہے لہذا عورت پر واجب ہے کہ ایسا ہرگز نہ کرے اگر کرے گی تو نکاح کالعدم ہونے کی وجہ سے ہمیشہ زنا میں مبتلا رہے گی۔
اسی سے اس صورت کا بھی حکم معلوم ہو گیا جس میں عورت کو شوہر کے غیر کفو ہونے کا علم نہ ہو یعنی عورت نے کفو ہونے کی شرط کرکے نکاح کیا اور بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ شوہر کفو نہیں ہے تو عورت پر واجب ہے کہ معلوم ہوتے ہی اس سے الگ ہو جائے کیوں کہ قول مفتی بہ کے موافق غیر کفو سے بغیر اذن ولی نکاح درست نہیں ہوتا تو جس وقت اس کا غیر کفو ہونا ظاہر ہو گیا اس وقت ثابت ہوگیا کہ نکاح اول ہی سے باطل تھا۔
دوسری صورت یہ کہ باپ دادا کے سوا کسی دوسرے ولی نے نابالغ کا نکاح غیر کفو میں کردیا ہو یا باپ دادا نے کیا مگر وہ معروف بسوء الاختیار فاسق مہتک ہو یا نشہ کی حالت میں نکاح کیا ہو اس صورت میں بھی نکاح بالکل باطل ہے۔
تیسری صورت یہ کہ باپ دادا نے ہوش میں غیر کفو میں نکاح کیا اور وہ باپ دادا فاسق مہتک نہ ہو اور معروف بسوء الاختیار نہیں ہے تو اس صورت میں نکاح صحیح اور لازم ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ حکم عام ہے خواہ باپ دادا کو نکاح کے وقت کفو نہ ہونے کا علم ہو یا نہیں دونوں صورتوں میں نکاح صحیح اور لازم ہوجاتا ہے البتہ اگر دوسری صورت یعنی عدم علم کی صورت میں کفؤ کی شرط پر نکاح کیا ہو تو اس کا حکم الگ ہے جو کہ چوتھی صورت میں آگے آرہا ہے۔
چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ بالغہ عورت کا نکاح ولی کی اجازت سے کفو نہ ہونے کا علم ہوتے ہوئے غیر کفو میں ہو تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ نکاح صحیح اور لازم ہو جاتا ہے اور کسی کو نکاح فسخ کرنے کا اختیار نہیں رہتا۔
There are several forms of marriage to a non-compatible spouse; in some the marriage is void, in some it is valid and binding (i.e. no right of rescission remains), and in some it is valid but not binding, rather the right of rescission remains. The actual purpose here is to mention those cases where there is an option of rescission because the need for qada of the qadi only arises in those, but for complete benefit we record all forms and write each separately. Their detail is as follows. First form: a mature woman marries a non-compatible spouse without the permission of a guardian. In this form the ruling is that the marriage is not valid but absolutely void; even if the guardian gives permission after the marriage, it is still not valid because prior permission is a condition. Therefore, it is obligatory upon the woman not to do this; if she does, she will remain in illegal intercourse due to the marriage being null. From this the ruling of that case is also known where the woman does not know of the husband's non-compatibility; i.e. she married stipulating compatibility and later learns the husband is not compatible; then it is obligatory upon her to separate from him as soon as she knows, because according to the preferred opinion, marriage to a non-compatible without guardian permission is not valid; so when his non-compatibility became apparent, it is established that the marriage was void from the beginning. Second form: a guardian other than the father or grandfather marries a minor to a non-compatible spouse, or the father/grandfather did it but he was notorious for evil choice, a wicked transgressor, or married in a state of intoxication; in this case the marriage is absolutely void. Third form: the father/grandfather, while sane, marries to a non-compatible, and that father/grandfather is not a wicked transgressor nor notorious for evil choice; then the marriage is valid and binding, and this ruling is general regardless of whether the father/grandfather knew at the time of marriage of the non-compatibility or not; in both cases the marriage is valid and binding. However, if in the second case (i.e. ignorance of non-compatibility) the marriage was contracted on condition of compatibility, then its ruling is separate, which will come in the fourth form. Fourth form: a mature woman's marriage to a non-compatible with the permission of a guardian while knowing the non-compatibility; the ruling is that the marriage is valid and binding, and no one has the right to rescind it.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a classification of rulings on marriages with a non-compatible spouse (ghayr kuf) in Hanafi fiqh. The author systematically lists four scenarios. First: a mature woman marries a non-compatible without any guardian's permission. This marriage is void (batil) ab initio, and even subsequent permission cannot validate it because the condition of prior permission is essential under the preferred opinion. The woman must separate immediately; otherwise, she remains in zina. The same applies if she married mistakenly thinking he was compatible but later discovered he was not — she must separate as soon as she learns. Second: if a guardian other than the father or grandfather (like a brother, uncle, etc.) marries a minor to a non-compatible, or if the father/grandfather does so while being fasiq mutahattik (notorious transgressor) or intoxicated, the marriage is also void. Third: if the father or grandfather, being of sound mind and not a wicked transgressor, marries the minor to a non-compatible, the marriage is valid and binding (lazim) even if the father was unaware of the non-compatibility. The exception is if the marriage was explicitly conditioned on compatibility — then it falls under the fourth form. Fourth: a mature woman with her guardian's permission marries a non-compatible while fully aware — this marriage is valid and binding with no option of rescission for anyone. The text clarifies that the purpose of mentioning all forms is to explain which ones allow judicial annulment, but for completeness all are listed.

Key Terms
غیر کفو (ghayr kuf): A spouse who is not equal in lineage, religion, wealth, profession, or other criteria of compatibility in marriage.
خیار فسخ (khiyar fasakh): The option to rescind a marriage contract due to a defect or lack of compatibility.
فاسق مہتک (fasiq mutahattik): A transgressor who is notorious for openly committing sins without regard for moral boundaries.
لازم (lazim): Binding; a marriage that is valid and cannot be annulled at will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mature woman marries a non-compatible spouse without her guardian's permission, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi preferred opinion in this passage?
A) The marriage is valid but the guardian can annul it.
B) The marriage is void (batil) and cannot be validated even by later permission.
C) The marriage is valid if the guardian later gives consent.
D) The marriage is suspended until the woman reaches puberty.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a marriage to a non-compatible spouse hinges on the guardian's permission and the guardian's probity; void marriages cannot be cured by later consent.

Khiyar al-Kufu' in Hanafi Marriage Law
Explaining the option of rescission for lack of equality in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on khiyar al-kufu' to both adult and minor marriage cases, distinguishing between virgins and non-virgins, and identify when silence voids the option.

Core Idea
The option to annul a non-kufu marriage is preserved only by immediate explicit objection; silence forfeits it for a virgin.

This passage from al-Hilat al-Najijah by Ashraf Ali Thanwi details the intricacies of khiyar al-kufu' (option of rescission due to lack of equality) in marriage. The author examines multiple scenarios: the effect of guardian type, virginity status, and the presence of conditions. Understanding these rulings is essential for a mufti when advising women or guardians who discover incompatibility after the marriage contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Determine who married: adult or minor, virgin or non-virgin, and who acted as guardian (father/grandfather or other). This sets the baseline for the khiyar ruling.
The guardian type matters: for a virgin married by father/grandfather, silence is consent; for others, explicit consent is needed.
2
Check the basis of the marriage
Was kufu' conditioned explicitly, or did the husband claim to be kufu'? Or did the guardian assume suitability without any statement? The presence of a condition or claim is necessary for khiyar.
If no condition or claim was made and the guardian acted on his own assumption, the existence of khiyar is disputed.
3
Apply the khiyar rule by status
For an adult virgin: she must object immediately upon discovery; silence voids the option. For a non-virgin: silence does not void; explicit or implicit consent (e.g., accepting dower) is required. For minors: before puberty, only father/grandfather has the option; after puberty, both child and guardian have independent options.
Implicit consent includes consummation or acceptance of dower.
4
Determine if khiyar is still valid
Check if any act of consent (explicit or implicit) has occurred after discovery. For a virgin, any delay or silence voids. For a non-virgin, look for dower acceptance or seclusion.
The option is preserved until consent is manifested.
5
Issue the fatwa
If khiyar exists and has not been voided, guide the party to seek annulment through a qadi. If khiyar is lost, the marriage becomes binding.
The mufti should ascertain the facts carefully, especially the timeline of discovery and actions.

Source Text

تمام اولیاء کے لیے عام ہے چاہے باپ دادا ہوں یا ان کے علاوہ کوئی دوسرا ولی ہو۔ لیکن فرق صرف یہ ہے کہ اگر لڑکی باکرہ ہے اور باپ دادا کی ولایت سے نکاح ہوا ہے تو اجازت کے لیے صرف لڑکی کا خاموش رہنا کافی ہوگا اور لڑکی ثیبہ (ہمبستری نشده) سے یا باپ دادا کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے ولی کی ولایت میں نکاح ہوا ہے تو اجازت کی ضرورت ہے محض خاموش رہنا کافی نہیں۔
بوقت نکاح کفارت پانچویں صورت یہ ہے کہ بالغہ عورت کا نکاح ولی کی اجازت سے کسی ایسے شخص سے ہوا کہ جس کی کفایت کا حال معلوم نہیں تھا لیکن نکاح کے وقت کفار کی شرط کر لی تھی یا واضح طور پر مشرط تو نہیں کی تھی لیکن شوہر کی طرف سے کفو ہونا ظاہر کیا گیا تھا اور اس پر اعتماد کر کے نکاح کر دیا ہو پھر خان ظاہر ہوا اور ثابت ہوا ہو کہ کفو نہیں ہے اس صورت کا حکم یہ ہے کہ عورت کو بھی خیار فسخ حاصل ہوگا اور اس کے ولی کو بھی، لیکن اگر یہ عورت ابھی تک باکرہ ہو تو اس کا خیار، خاموش رہنے سے باطل ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی اگر معلوم ہونے کے بعد فوراً کہہ دیا کہ مجھ کو اس شخص سے نکاح باقی رکھنا منظور نہیں جب تو اختیار باقی رہے گا اور بذریعہ حکم مسلم، نکاح فسخ کر سکے گی، ورنہ اگر نامنظوری ظاہر کرنے میں کچھ بھی تاخیر کر دی تو خیار فسخ باقی نہیں رہے گا۔
یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جب کہ لڑکی باکرہ ہو۔ اور اگر لڑکی ثیبہ ہوچکی ہے ہو اور لڑکی عاملہ شوہر کس و تعدیل کرے (یعنی بوسہ ہے یا چھوٹے) یا مہر اور ہفتہ ادا کر دے اور پیری اس کو چھوٹے یا بوسہ وغیرہ پر قدرت دستے یا مہر وغیرہ قبول کرنے کو یہ دلالہ رضا مندی ہے اور جبر کا ہوں کرنا اس وقت دلیلی رضا ہے جبکہ بالغ ہونے سے پہلے خلوت صحیحہ نہ ہو چکی ہوں تو اس کے خاموش رہنے سے اختیار باطل نہیں ہوتا جب تک صراحتہ یا دلالہ رضا مندی نہ پائی جائے اُس وقت تک اختیار باقی رہے گا اور یہی حکم ولی کا اس کا خیار فسخ بھی محض خاموشی سے باطل نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صراحتہ یا دلالہ کی مناکی ضرورت ہے۔ اور دلالہ رضا کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مثلا عورت مہر وغیرہ پر قبضہ کر لے۔
چھٹی صورت یہ ہے کہ نابالغ لڑکے یا لڑکی نکاح اس کے باپ یا دادا نے ایسے شخص سے کیا جس کو اس کے بیان کی بنا پر کفو سمجھ گیا تھا یا کفو ہونے کی شرط کر لی گئی تھی یا بد میں معلوم ہوا کہ غیر کفو ہے اس صورت میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ بالغ ہونے سے پیشتر تو صرف باپ دادا کو اختیار ہے اگر اس نے فسخ نکاح کروایا تو فسخ ہو جائے گا اور اگر حقیقت ظاہر ہونے کے بعد بھی نکاح کو منظور رکھا تو لازم ہو جائے گا اور اگر باپ دادا نے سکوت کیا تو صرف اس کے سکوت سے اختیار باطل نہ ہوگا بلکہ باپ دادا کو بھی اختیار باقی ہے اور بالغ ہونے پر لڑکے لڑکی کو بھی اختیار حاصل ہو جائے گا اس لیے بالغ ہونے کے بعد نکاح لازم ہونے کے واسطے دونوں کی رضا مندی شرط ہے باپ دادا کی بھی اور لڑکے لڑکی کی بھی۔ پس بلوغ کے بعد لڑکے یا لڑکی اور باپ یا دادا میں سے ایک بھی چاہے تو نکاح فسخ ہو سکتا ہے، اگرچہ دوسرا باقی رہنے پر راضی ہو جائے۔
علی ہذا بعون وجنونہ کا بیٹا ان احکام میں باپ کے برابر ہے جیسا کہ بیشتر گذر چکا۔ بیان علی اگر کفاومت کی شرط نہ کی تھی اور نہ زوج نے اپنا کفو ہونا بیان کیا تھا بلکہ باپ دادا نے محض اپنے گمان سے کفو سمجھ کر نکاح کر دیا تھا پھر ظاہر ہوا کہ کفو نہیں تو اس صورت میں خیار کفارت ہوتے ہیں بوجود تبع اور مراجعت علماء کو کوئی امر نفع ہوسکا اور نہیں قواعد سے رحجان اس کو معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اس صورت میں خیار فسخ نہ دیا جائے مگر عمل کے وقت اہل علم ان جزئیات کو دیکھ کر جن کا حوالہ اصل تمہ کے حاشیہ پر درج ہے کسی جانب کو خود ترجیح دیں ہارتا بیچ پر نہ رہیں
This is general for all guardians, whether fathers, grandfathers, or someone else. But the only difference is that if the girl is a virgin and the marriage is contracted under the guardianship of the father or grandfather, then for permission, only her silence is sufficient. And if the girl is a non-virgin (who has not had intercourse) or the marriage is contracted under the guardianship of someone other than the father or grandfather, then permission is needed; mere silence is not sufficient.
The fifth scenario at the time of marriage: that an adult woman's marriage is contracted with the permission of a guardian to a person whose status of suitability (kafa'ah) was not known, but at the time of marriage, suitability was made a condition, or it was not explicitly conditioned but the husband claimed to be a suitable match, and relying on that, the marriage was performed. Then later it became apparent and proven that he is not suitable. The ruling of this scenario is that the woman and her guardian both have the option of rescission (khiyar al-faskh). But if this woman is still a virgin, her option becomes void by silence. That is, if immediately after discovering she explicitly says, 'I do not wish to remain in this marriage,' then the option remains and she can have the marriage annulled through a Muslim judge. Otherwise, if there is any delay in expressing disapproval, the option of rescission ceases to exist.
This ruling is when the girl is a virgin. And if the girl has become a non-virgin and the girl [؟] the husband kisses or touches, or pays the dower and [؟] and she accepts the dower, this indicates consent. And [؟] at that time is further evidence of consent provided that a valid seclusion had not occurred before puberty. Then her silence does not void the option until explicit or implicit consent is found; until then the option remains. And the same ruling applies to the guardian's option of rescission; it is not voided by mere silence, but explicit or implicit consent is needed. The form of implicit consent is, for example, that the woman takes possession of the dower.
The sixth scenario: that a minor boy or girl is married by his/her father or grandfather to a person whom, based on his statement, he considered suitable, or suitability was conditioned, but later it became known that he is not suitable. In this scenario, the detail is that before attaining puberty, only the father or grandfather has the option. If he has the marriage annulled, it will be annulled; and if after the fact becomes apparent he approves the marriage, it becomes binding. And if the father or grandfather remains silent, the option is not voided by his silence alone; rather, the father or grandfather retains the option. Upon reaching puberty, the boy and girl also acquire the option. Therefore, after puberty, for the marriage to be binding, the consent of both is required: the father/grandfather and the boy/girl. So after puberty, if any one of them—the boy/girl or the father/grandfather—desires, the marriage can be annulled, even if the other is satisfied with its continuation.
Similarly, the son of a paternal uncle and [؟] in these rulings are equal to the father, as has mostly passed. Explanation: if suitability was not conditioned and the husband did not claim to be suitable, but rather the father or grandfather, based on his own assumption, considered him suitable and contracted the marriage, then later it becomes apparent that he is not suitable, then in this scenario, [khiyar] [؟] exist. And [؟] scholars [؟] nothing benefits. And from the principles, it appears that in this scenario, khiyar al-faskh should not be granted. But at the time of practice, scholars, looking at these details whose reference is given in the footnote of the original [؟], should give preference themselves and not remain confused.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage from al-Hilat al-Najijah details the rulings of khiyar al-kufu' (option of rescission due to lack of equality) in marriage. The author discusses several scenarios. First, the general rule: all guardians have similar jurisdiction, but the effect of silence differs: for a virgin married by father/grandfather, silence is consent; for a non-virgin or marriage by other guardians, explicit or implicit consent is needed. Fifth scenario: an adult woman marries with guardian's permission under a condition of kufu or based on the husband's claim; upon discovering non-suitability, both woman and guardian have khiyar. However, if the woman is a virgin, her khiyar is lost by silence; she must object immediately. For a non-virgin, silence does not void her option until she explicitly or implicitly consents (e.g., accepting dower). Sixth scenario: minor children are married by father/grandfather based on a claim or condition of kufu. Before puberty, only the father/grandfather has the option; after puberty, both the child and the father/grandfather each have independent option. Finally, if no condition or claim was made, and the father/grandfather acted on his own assumption, the text notes a difference of opinion: the preferred view suggests no khiyar, but scholars should examine the details. The passage emphasizes that the khiyar is subject to conditions and varies with the status of the woman (virgin/non-virgin) and the guardian.

Key Terms
کفو (kufu): Equality in social status, lineage, religion, and other criteria relevant to marriage compatibility.
خیار فسخ (khiyar al-faskh): Option to annul the marriage contract due to a defect or lack of condition.
باکره (bikr): A virgin girl who has never been married.
ثیبه (thayyib): A non-virgin woman, whether divorced or widowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Remaining silent for a few days
B) Accepting the dower from her husband
C) Seeking advice from her guardian

Key Takeaway
The khiyar al-faskh for non-kufu' is governed by distinct rules based on the woman's virginity and the type of guardian; a mufti must apply these distinctions carefully.

Marriage with Kitabiyyah: Conditions and Ruling
Rulings on pre-marriage religious difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for a Muslim man to marry a Kitabiyyah woman and explain why such marriage is makruh without necessity.

Core Idea
A Muslim man may marry a Kitabiyyah only if she is original and believing; such marriage is makruh unless necessary.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on pre-existing religious difference between spouses. The rule is clear: a Muslim woman can never marry a non-Muslim, and a Muslim man cannot marry a disbelieving woman unless she is a Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian) and meets two strict conditions. Even then, the marriage is discouraged (makruh) due to spiritual risks, as emphasized by Caliph Umar's prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the universal prohibition
Note that the marriage of a Muslim woman to any non-Muslim man is absolutely forbidden, regardless of his religion. Similarly, a Muslim man is prohibited from marrying a non-Muslim woman unless she is Kitabiyyah.
This is a foundational rule in Hanafi fiqh.
2
State the two conditions for Kitabiyyah marriage
First, the woman must genuinely adhere to her religious principles, not merely nominal as seen in some European nations. Second, she must be originally Jewish or Christian, not an apostate from Islam.
Condition 2 excludes those who converted from Islam to Kitabiyyah.
3
Understand the ruling when conditions are met
When both conditions are present, the marriage is valid (sahih) and contracted. However, without severe necessity (darura), it is makruh and contains many evils.
The author cites the example of Caliph Umar's prohibition to illustrate the harm.
4
Apply the rule to a modern scenario
Consider a Muslim man in a Western country wanting to marry a Christian woman who is born Christian and practices her faith. This meets the conditions. But assess necessity: if no necessity, the marriage is makruh.
The mufti must weigh the social and religious consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِسْمِ اللهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمُ
مذہب زوجین کے اختلاف کی دو صورتیں ہیں ایک یہ کہ یہ اختلاف نکاح سے پہلے ہی دو موجودہ ہو دوسرے یہ کہ بعد نکاح پیدا ہو جائے۔ پہلی صورت میں مسلمان عورت کا نکاح کسی کافر سے کسی حالت میں جائز نہیں چاہتے کر کی کوئی قسم ہو اس طریقہ سے مسلمان مرد کا نکاح بھی کسی کا فرعورت سے جائز نہیں۔ البتہ اگر عورت کتابیہ یعنی۔ یہودیہ یا نصرانیہ و غیرہ ہو تو اس سے مسلمان مرد کا نکاح دو شرائط کے ساتھ ہو سکتا ہے۔ اول یہ کہ وہ اقوام یورپ کی طرح صرف نام کی عیسائی اور حقیقت میں رہا مذہب) نے وہر یہ نہ ہو بلکہ اپنے مذہبی اصو کو کم از کم مانتی ہیں اگر یہ عمل میں غایت بھی کرتی ہو۔ دوسرے یہ کہ وہ اصل سے ہی یہودیہ یا نصرانیہ ہو، اسلام سے مرتد ہو کر یہودیت یا نصرانیت اختیار نہ کی ہو۔ جس وقت یہ دونوں شرائط کسی کتابیہ عورت میں پائی جائیں تو اس سے نکاح صحیح و منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ لیکن بلا ضرورت شدیدہ اس سے میں نکاح کرنا مکروہ ہے اور بہت سی خرابیوں پر مشتمل ہے اس لیے حضرت فاروق اعظم رضی اللہ عنہ نے اپنے دور خلافت میں مسلمانوں کو کتابیہ عورتوں کے نکاح سے منع فرمایا تھا اور جب عہد فاروقی میں کہ زمانہ خیر تھا ایسے مفاسد موجود تھے تو آج جس قدر مفاسد ہوں کم ہیں خصوصاً موجودہ اقوام یورپ کے ساتھ مسلمانوں کے تعلقات ازدواج کو بالکل ہی اپنے دین اور دنیا کو تباہ کر دینے والے ہیں جن کا روز مرہ مشاہدہ ہوتا ہے۔
دوسری صورت بود نکاح شوہر بیوی میں سے کسی کے کافر ہونے کی چار صورتیں یعنی نکاح کے بعد زوجین کا یا ان میں سے کسی ایک کا مذہب بدل جائے اس کے چار احتمال ہیں۔ یعنی چار صورتیں ہیں) پہلا احتمال یہ ہے کہ دونوں کا فر تھے پھر ایک ساتھ دونوں مسلمان ہو گئے۔ دوسرا احتمال یہ ہے کہ دونوں مسلمن تھے پھر معاذ اللہ دونوں ایک ساتھ مرتد ہو گئے۔ ان دونوں احتمالات میں نکاح پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑتا بلکہ نکاح بعنیہ قائم رہتا ہے۔ تیسرا احتمال یعنی تیسری صورت یہ ہے کہ دونوں میں سے کوئی ایک مسلمان ہو جائے اور دوسرا بدستور کفر پر باقی رہے اس کے دو اجزاء میں ایک یہ کہ مرد مسلمان ہو جائے اور عورت کفر پر ہے تو اس صورت کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر عورت کتابیہ ہے تو نکاح پر کوئی اثر نہ پڑے گا نکاح بحالہ قائم رہے گا۔ اگر چہ وہ اہل کتاب کا ایک مذہب چھوڑ کر دوسر مذہب اختیار کرے، مثلاً یہودیہ سے نصرانیہ (عیسائی) ہو جائے یا اس کا عکس یعنی عسائی سے یہودی بن جائے اسی طرح سے اگر ایسا ہو کہ جس وقت مرد مسلمان ہو رہے اسی وقت مجوسیہ نے اہل کتاب کا مذہب قبول کر لیا اس صورت میں بھی نکاح پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑتا۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. There are two forms of difference of religion between spouses: one is that this difference exists before marriage, and the other is that it occurs after marriage. In the first form, the marriage of a Muslim woman to any disbeliever is never permissible in any condition, regardless of his type. Similarly, the marriage of a Muslim man to a disbelieving woman is also not permissible. However, if the woman is a Kitabiyyah, i.e., Jewish or Christian etc., then a Muslim man can marry her with two conditions. First, that she is not merely a nominal Christian like the European nations who are in reality without religion, but she at least believes in her religious principles, even if she is extreme in practice. Second, that she is originally Jewish or Christian, and did not become Jewish or Christian by apostasy from Islam. When these two conditions are found in a Kitabiyyah woman, then marriage with her is valid and contracted. But without severe necessity, marrying her is Makruh and contains many evils. Therefore, Caliph Umar al-Azam (RA) prohibited Muslims from marrying Kitabiyyah women during his caliphate. And when in the era of Umar, which was a good time, such evils existed, then today there are many evils, especially the marital relations of Muslims with the current European nations are entirely destructive to their religion and world, as is observed daily. The second form is after marriage: the four scenarios of one of the spouses becoming a disbeliever, i.e., after marriage, the religion of the couple or one of them changes. There are four probabilities (i.e., four scenarios). The first probability: both were disbelievers, then together both became Muslims. The second probability: both were Muslims, then (God forbid) both apostatized together. In both these probabilities, there is no effect on the marriage; rather the marriage remains as it is. The third probability (i.e., third scenario) is that one of them becomes Muslim while the other remains upon disbelief. Of this, there are two subcases: one is that the man becomes Muslim while the woman remains upon disbelief. The ruling in this case is that if the woman is a Kitabiyyah, then marriage is unaffected; the marriage will remain in force. Even if she leaves one religion of the People of the Book and adopts another, e.g., from Jewish to Christian, or vice versa. Similarly, if at the time the man becomes Muslim, the Zoroastrian woman adopts the religion of the People of the Book, in this case also the marriage is unaffected.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a summary (خلاصه) of Hanafi rulings on the effect of religious difference between spouses, both before and after marriage. The author divides the topic into two main scenarios. The first scenario covers pre-existing difference: a Muslim woman may never marry a non-Muslim man; a Muslim man may only marry a Kitabiyyah (Jewish or Christian) woman under two strict conditions: she must genuinely adhere to her revealed religion (not merely nominal), and she must have been originally Kitabiyyah, not an apostate from Islam. Even then, such marriage is Makruh unless necessary, and the author notes Caliph Umar's prohibition due to spiritual and worldly harms. The second scenario addresses changes after marriage: if both convert to Islam together or both apostatize together, marriage remains intact. When only one spouse converts and the other remains a disbeliever, the ruling depends on whether the remaining spouse is Kitabiyyah. The text emphasizes that these rulings are practical guidelines for a mufti issuing fatwas in such cases.

Key Terms
کتابیہ (Kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book (Jewish or Christian) who believes in her revealed scripture and is not an apostate from Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which two conditions must be met for a Muslim man to marry a Kitabiyyah woman?
A) She must be a virgin and she must convert to Islam.
B) She must be originally Kitabiyyah and she must believe in her religious principles.
C) She must be from Arabia and she must be a descendant of the Prophet.
D) She must be wealthy and her family must consent.

Key Takeaway
A Muslim man may marry a Kitabiyyah woman only if she is originally from the People of the Book and genuinely believes; such marriage is valid but makruh without severe necessity.
